<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Greensboro Coliseum Complex</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p>The <b>Greensboro Coliseum Complex</b> (formerly known as <b>Greensboro Coliseum</b>) is an entertainment and sports complex located in <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro, North Carolina</a>. Opening in 1959, the arena was once one of the largest venues in the South, with a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of over 23,000. The complex holds eight venues that includes an amphitheater, arena, aquatic center, banquet hall, convention center, museum, theatre and an indoor pavilion. It is the home of the <a href="/wiki/UNC_Greensboro_Spartans_men%27s_basketball" title="UNC Greensboro Spartans men's basketball">University of North Carolina at Greensboro's "Spartans"</a> men's basketball team, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> (ACC) with their <a href="/wiki/ACC_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="ACC Men's Basketball Tournament">Men's</a> and <a href="/wiki/ACC_Women%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="ACC Women's Basketball Tournament">Women's</a> Basketball Tournament.</p>
<p>It has hosted the Men's ACC Tournament twenty-three times since 1967 and the Women's ACC Tournament twelve times since 2000. The Coliseum hosted both tournaments until 2015. Other notable sporting events include the <a href="/wiki/1974_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1974 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">National Collegiate Athletic Association (NCAA) Men's "Final Four"</a> in 1974 and the East Regionals in <a href="/wiki/1976_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament#Locations" title="1976 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1976</a>, <a href="/wiki/1979_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament#Locations" title="1979 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1979</a> and <a href="/wiki/1998_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament#Locations" title="1998 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1998</a>. It is also the former home of several professional hockey teams including the <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Generals" title="Greensboro Generals">Greensboro Generals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Monarchs" title="Greensboro Monarchs">Greensboro Monarchs</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Coast_Hockey_League" title="East Coast Hockey League">East Coast Hockey League</a> (ECHL) and the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Hurricanes" title="Carolina Hurricanes">Carolina Hurricanes</a>. It is also the current home of the <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Swarm" title="Greensboro Swarm">Greensboro Swarm</a> of the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Development_League" title="NBA Development League">NBA Development League</a>.</p>
<p>The complex has hosted the "Central Carolina Fair" since 1999.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GreensboroColiseumnasa.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="992" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/GreensboroColiseumnasa.png/200px-GreensboroColiseumnasa.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/GreensboroColiseumnasa.png/300px-GreensboroColiseumnasa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/GreensboroColiseumnasa.png/400px-GreensboroColiseumnasa.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GreensboroColiseumnasa.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of complex showing the coliseum, exhibition hall, performing arts center and theatre (2007).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The complex was first proposed in 1944 by the city's mayor. The idea was to create a <a href="/wiki/War_memorial" title="War memorial">war memorial</a> to honor veterans of World War I and World War II. The building was approved by city officials in 1956, followed by a groundbreaking in January 1958. With its opening in 1959, the complex held four venues: <b>War Memorial Auditorium</b>, <b>Town Hall Auditorium</b>, <b>The Blue Room</b> and the <b>Greensboro Coliseum</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-history-2">[2]</a></sup> The complex opened on October 29, 1959 for historic show, "<a href="/wiki/Holiday_on_Ice" title="Holiday on Ice">Holiday on Ice</a>". Shortly after its opening, the Coliseum began to scout for a hockey team. Partnering with the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hockey_League" title="Eastern Hockey League">EHL</a>, the city formed the "Greensboro Generals". The team's first match was November 11, 1959 against the Washington Presidents. The Generals won the game 4–1. The Generals would go on to win the EHL Championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-history-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the years, the complex hosted several conventions, sporting and musical events. The Coliseum was part-time home of the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Cougars" title="Carolina Cougars">Carolina Cougars</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association" title="American Basketball Association">American Basketball Association</a> from 1969 to 1974 after the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Mavericks" title="Houston Mavericks">Houston Mavericks</a> moved to North Carolina in 1969. The Cougars were a "regional franchise," playing "home" games in Charlotte (<a href="/wiki/Bojangles%27_Coliseum" title="Bojangles' Coliseum">Bojangles' Coliseum</a>), Greensboro (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greensboro_Coliseum" title="Greensboro Coliseum">Greensboro Coliseum</a>), <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Winston-Salem Memorial Coliseum">Winston-Salem Memorial Coliseum</a> and Raleigh (<a href="/wiki/Dorton_Arena" title="Dorton Arena">Dorton Arena</a>). Hall of Fame Coach <a href="/wiki/Larry_Brown_(basketball)" title="Larry Brown (basketball)">Larry Brown</a> began his coaching career with the Cougars in 1972. <a href="/wiki/Billy_Cunningham" title="Billy Cunningham">Billy Cunningham</a> was the ABA MVP for the Cougars in the 1972-73 season. Despite a strong fan base the Cougars were sold and moved to St. Louis in 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>To meet demands, the Coliseum expanded its seating to 15,000 in 1972. Six years later, the complex expanded to include an exhibition center, known at the time as the <b>Greensboro Coliseum Complex Exhibition Building</b> (shortened to Exhibition Building). The building's first event was "Super Flea", a <a href="/wiki/Flea_market" title="Flea market">flea market</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_Triad" title="Piedmont Triad">Triad area</a>. In 1991, the Coliseum's manager (Jim Evans) proposed an additional expansion of the complex. This expansion would raise the <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of the Coliseum an additional 8,000 (adding a third tier) to 23,000. It would also see The Blue Room demolished to make way for a small arena in the Exhibition Hall (now called the <b>Special Events Center</b>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The venue reopened in December 28, 1993 for the "Reunion Classic", a men's basketball game between the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins_men%27s_basketball" title="UCLA Bruins men's basketball">UCLA Bruins</a> and <a href="/wiki/NC_State_Wolfpack_men%27s_basketball" title="NC State Wolfpack men's basketball">NC State Wolfpack</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> This game was met with controversy as the Coliseum was not fully complete at the time of the game. City officials paid $200,000 to have firefighters on stand by during the game. The Coliseum and the newly expanded exhibition hall did not meet state and city building codes nor fire regulations, because of incomplete construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fire_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-fire-6">[6]</a></sup> Additionally, the Coliseum did not hold the permits to host the event. This decision resulted in city council firing both the Coliseum manager and its contractors, Huber, Hunt and Nichols, Inc. (known for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable_Arena" title="Time Warner Cable Arena">Time Warner Cable Arena</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BB%26T_Center_(Sunrise)" title="BB&amp;T Center (Sunrise)">BB&amp;T Center (Sunrise)</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consol_Energy_Center" title="Consol Energy Center">Consol Energy Center</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fire_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-fire-6">[6]</a></sup> It was later determined it would take an additional ten months to have the complex comply with regulations. The city added in additional $20 million to the budget to renovate the Coliseum and the auditorium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Additional expansions came in 2003 when the complex added the 30,000 sqft <b>Pavilion</b> (also called the <b>GCC Pavilion</b>). Two years later, the complex would renovated the old Town Hall Auditorium into the smaller <b>Odeon Theatre</b>. In 2011, the complex added three additional venues: the <b>White Oak Amphitheatre</b>, the <b>Greensboro Aquatic Center</b> and the <b>ACC Hall of Champions</b>. Since its opening, the complex has been visited by nearly 57 million people and hosts over 800 events per year.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greensboro_Coliseum">Greensboro Coliseum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Greensboro Coliseum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the original four buildings of the complex, the Coliseum (also called Coliseum Arena) is one of the oldest buildings on the property. Construction began on the venue in 1958 and was completed in September 1959. Known originally as the Greensboro Memorial Coliseum (until 1980), the arena hosted its first event on October 29, 1959. At the time, the Coliseum held 7,100 seats, becoming one of the largest arenas on the East Coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Less than one year after its opening, the Coliseum was about to be visited by presidential nominee <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>. Nixon sustained a knee injury while campaigning in Greensboro, causing him to stop his campaign tour. Although the tour continued in late August 1960, Nixon still suffered pain from the injury. In September, the first debate between <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> and Nixon aired on television, with Nixon appearing to look "sickly". Nixon lost the debate and would go on to lose the presidential race. Nixon later stated the knee injury at the Coliseum resulted in him losing the race.</p>
<p>Through the years, the Coliseum has hosted several sporting events, most notably basketball (see below). The Coliseum has also hosted concerts for over 40 years. During the 1960s and 1970s, the Coliseum was frequented by rock and R&amp;B performers. The first major concert held at the Coliseum was by <a href="/wiki/The_Monkees" title="The Monkees">The Monkees</a>. <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> played a concert at the Coliseum on April 14, 1972; the footage was used for his final film, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Elvis_on_Tour" title="Elvis on Tour">Elvis on Tour</a></i> and an audio album, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley_%E2%80%93_The_Greensboro_Concert_1972" title="Elvis Presley – The Greensboro Concert 1972">Elvis Presley – The Greensboro Concert 1972</a></i>. Presley performed the Coliseum again on April 21, 1977, one of the final venues of his tour, before his death on August 16. <a href="/wiki/Casting_Crowns" title="Casting Crowns">Casting Crowns</a> recorded their live album, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Until_the_Whole_World_Hears..._Live" title="Until the Whole World Hears... Live">Until the Whole World Hears... Live</a></i>, at the Coliseum on April 24, 2010.</p>
<p>The arena has also hosted <a href="/wiki/WJMH" title="WJMH">WJMH</a>'s <a href="/wiki/102_JAMZ_SuperJam" title="102 JAMZ SuperJam">SuperJam</a> since 1997. The music festival has featured prominent artists in the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> community including <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soulja_Boy" title="Soulja Boy">Soulja Boy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plies_(rapper)" title="Plies (rapper)">Plies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lil_Jon_%26_the_East_Side_Boyz" title="Lil Jon &amp; the East Side Boyz">Lil Jon &amp; the East Side Boyz</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Travis_Porter_(group)" title="Travis Porter (group)">Travis Porter</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ying_Yang_Twins" title="Ying Yang Twins">Ying Yang Twins</a>.</p>
<p>The Coliseum was also the site of auditions for <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_5)" title="American Idol (season 5)">Season 5</a> on October 3, 2005. Between Sunday, July 8 and Tuesday, July 10, 2012, it played host to the Greensboro audition stages in the second season of the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> singer search program <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The X Factor (U.S. TV series)">The X Factor</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_Memorial_Auditorium">War Memorial Auditorium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: War Memorial Auditorium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the original four buildings of the complex, the War Memorial Auditorium was one of the oldest buildings on the property, until it was razed in 2014. Along with the original concept, the venue opened in 1959 to house performing arts events. Playing predominately to an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> audience, the auditorium became a notable venue on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chitlin%27_circuit" title="Chitlin' circuit">chitlin' circuit</a>. <a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Charles" title="Ray Charles">Ray Charles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a> were among the many performers who played the auditorium during the 1960s. <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> played the auditorium during the band's <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones_2nd_American_Tour_1965" title="The Rolling Stones 2nd American Tour 1965">1965 North American Tour</a> on November 12, 1965. The venue was primarily used for town meetings, theatrical events, religious meetings and concerts. Presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> held a <a href="/wiki/Town_hall_meeting" title="Town hall meeting">town hall meeting</a> on March 26, 2008 to a full house. <a href="/wiki/Guilford_County,_North_Carolina" title="Guilford County, North Carolina">Guilford County</a> native <a href="/wiki/Fantasia_Barrino" title="Fantasia Barrino">Fantasia Barrino</a> gave her first concert, in her home state, during her <a href="/wiki/Back_to_Me_Tour" title="Back to Me Tour">Back to Me Tour</a> on November 18, 2010.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The auditorium was torn down in October 2014; a premium parking lot planned on the site will subsidize the <a href="/wiki/Steven_Tanger_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Steven Tanger Center for the Performing Arts">Steven Tanger Center for the Performing Arts</a>, to open downtown as a replacement facility in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killian_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Killian-11">[11]</a></sup> A closing ceremony took place September 4. An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O%27Jays" title="O'Jays">O'Jays</a> concert September 5 was the last event, and items from the auditorium were auctioned off the next week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greensboro_Coliseum_Special_Events_Center">Greensboro Coliseum Special Events Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Greensboro Coliseum Special Events Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Originally known as the Greensboro Coliseum Complex Exhibition Building, the exhibition center opened in 1978. Its purpose was to host business conferences and conventions. The venue was primarily used by "Super Flea", the flea market for the Triad area. In 1993, the center was expanded, converting the old Blue Room into a mid-sized <a href="/wiki/Arena" title="Arena">arena</a> known as <b>Hall C</b> or the <b>East Wing</b>. In its current state, the 167,000-square foot center "includes three exhibition halls, a 4,500-seat mini-arena and eight meeting rooms...."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The arena is often used for musical performances during the Central Carolina Fair. It is also utilized by <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_College" title="Greensboro College">Greensboro College</a> men's and women's basketball home games. Other sporting events include <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC matches</a>. The arena will often host concerts and comedy shows.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Odeon_Theatre">Odeon Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Odeon Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Opening in 1958 as the Town Hall Auditorium, the Odeon Theatre is a small venue primarily used for community events. The original auditorium housed 1,000 seats. In 2004, the auditorium was converted to the smaller theatre and reopened in March 2005.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="White_Oak_Amphitheatre">White Oak Amphitheatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: White Oak Amphitheatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The newest addition to the complex, the White Oak Amphitheatre is the first outdoor venue for the Triad area. The venue was originally proposed in 2007 along with the aquatic center. The city purchased the nearby <a href="/wiki/Canada_Dry" title="Canada Dry">Canada Dry</a> bottling plant to allow space for the amphitheatre. Construction began in 2010 and was completed in June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The first concert for the venue was by <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">The Beach Boys</a> on June 5, 2011 to a crowd of 4,000 spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The amphitheatre is expected to operate from April to October, hosting community, comedy and musical events. The project cost $946,000 to construct.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fieldhouse">Fieldhouse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Fieldhouse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Known simply by one name (although acknowledged as <b>Greensboro Coliseum Fieldhouse</b>), the Fieldhouse is a standalone exhibition hall adjacent to the Special Events Center. The 30,000 sq ft space is used monthly by the Super Flea Market. It also is used frequently by Guilford County Schools and the Central Carolina Fair. The Fieldhouse opened in March 2003. The project was designed by Sutton-Kennerly Associates and cost $625,606. Starting in 2016, the Fieldhouse will be the home to the <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Swarm" title="Greensboro Swarm">Greensboro Swarm</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Development_League" title="NBA Development League">NBA Development League</a> affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets" title="Charlotte Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</a>. To accommodate the team the Fieldhouse will be renovated into a basketball fieldhouse with a permanent roof, new locker room, and seating of 2,118.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greensboro_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greensboro-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greensboro_Aquatic_Center">Greensboro Aquatic Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Greensboro Aquatic Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Another expansion project for the complex is the new aquatic center. The center features three main pools including a warm-up and training pool. The main pool will be used for events by nearby high schools and colleges and can hold eight 50-meter lanes. The facility also has a classroom and a 24'×19' video screen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The venue will house events in <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">competitive swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" title="Synchronized swimming">synchronized swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>. The project began in 2010 along with the amphitheatre and cost $18.8 million to build.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The City of Greensboro provided a live cam feed to watch the progress of the construction. The venue is expected to open in August 2011. The venue has hosted the 2012 U.S. Masters Swimming Spring National Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Precise_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated.">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup>, the 2015 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Swimming_and_Diving_Championships" title="NCAA Women's Division I Swimming and Diving Championships">NCAA Women's Division I Swimming and Diving Championships</a>, and other tournaments as well.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ACC_Hall_of_Champions">ACC Hall of Champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: ACC Hall of Champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To commemorate its legacy with the ACC Tournaments, the complex opened a museum in 2011 to show the history of the ACC. The venue will celebrate the past, present and future of the ACC. It features numerous exhibits including an interactive broadcast booth, memorabilia, a video globe and school mascots. The venue opened in March 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acc_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-acc-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Terrace">The Terrace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Terrace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Opened in March 2011, The Terrace is one of new expansions for the complex. Its main purpose is a banquet hall and will be used for speaking events as well as weddings. The Terrace is an indoor venue located in between the auditorium and Coliseum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acc_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-acc-21">[21]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hockey">Hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The hockey history of Greensboro began in 1959, when the Greensboro Generals of the Eastern Hockey League arrived and competed until the league folded in 1973. The team moved to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Hockey_League_(1973%E2%80%931977)" title="Southern Hockey League (1973–1977)">Southern Hockey League</a> for four seasons until it too ceased operations in January 1977.</p>
<p>Greensboro hockey's modern era began with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Monarchs" title="Greensboro Monarchs">Greensboro Monarchs</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Coast_Hockey_League" title="East Coast Hockey League">East Coast Hockey League</a>, who played from 1989–90 to 1994–95. When the <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">American Hockey League</a> expanded southward in 1995, it invited Greensboro to join; the new team took the Monarchs nickname, but attempted to draw a more regional fan base by labeling themselves the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Monarchs" title="Carolina Monarchs">Carolina Monarchs</a>.</p>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Hartford_Whalers" title="Hartford Whalers">Hartford Whalers</a> announced their move to <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh, North Carolina</a> in 1997 (which they are now known as the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Hurricanes" title="Carolina Hurricanes">Carolina Hurricanes</a>), they leased the Coliseum for two years while waiting for the <a href="/wiki/PNC_Arena" title="PNC Arena">Raleigh Entertainment and Sports Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh, North Carolina</a> to be completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Subjected to ticket price increases and unwilling to support a team that was destined for Raleigh, Greensboro hockey fans rarely filled the arena for Hurricane games. Meanwhile, Triangle fans were unwilling to make the hour-long drive across <a href="/wiki/Interstate_40" title="Interstate 40">Interstate 40</a> to Greensboro. As a result, the Hurricanes played in front of some of the smallest NHL crowds since the 1950s. During the 1998–99 season, the team curtained off most of the upper deck for home games in an effort to artificially create scarcity in the ticket market, force would-be attendees to purchase higher-priced tickets, and hide what national media mocked as "green acres" of empty seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Once the Raleigh Entertainment and Sports Arena (later the RBC Center, now the PNC Arena) was completed and the Hurricanes moved out, the plan was that the Monarchs, who spent those two years in <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven, Connecticut</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Beast_of_New_Haven" title="Beast of New Haven">Beast of New Haven</a>, would move back into the venue as a Hurricanes affiliate. However, Monarchs owner Bill Black tried to bring the Monarchs back to Greensboro but the Hurricanes refused to claim the Monarchs as their affiliate. After the deal fell by the wayside Bill Black tried to sell shares to the public in a final attempt to bring the Monarchs back to Greensboro. Unable to regain enough interest the team was sold and became the Manchester Monarchs.</p>
<p>Rather than leave the Coliseum without a hockey team for the first time in more than 10 years, a new hockey team was founded, the <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Generals" title="Greensboro Generals">Greensboro Generals</a>, returning the city to the East Coast Hockey League. The Generals competed in the arena until 2004, when they were terminated by the ECHL due to poor performance and lackluster support from the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Increased operating expenses from the ECHL Players Union and overhead costs as a result of recent Coliseum renovations significantly affected the Generals' ability to promote within the community. It was revealed that after the team folded, nearly all of the money used to support the team over and above ticket revenues, could have been covered by Coliseum advertising revenue that was purchased as a direct result of the hockey team's presence. After the team folded, the complex saw a significant revenue drop in local advertising and to this day, the Coliseum operations must be supplemented with nearly $2 million a year from the city government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Cougars" title="Carolina Cougars">Carolina Cougars</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(1967%E2%80%931976)" title="American Basketball Association (1967–1976)">American Basketball Association</a> played a majority of their home games at the Greensboro Coliseum during their tenure in North Carolina from 1969 to 1974, before moving to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a> and becoming the <a href="/wiki/Spirits_of_St._Louis" title="Spirits of St. Louis">Spirits of St. Louis</a>. The Greensboro City Gaters played their first and only season as a charter franchise of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Basketball_Association" title="Global Basketball Association">Global Basketball Association</a> minor league in 1991–1992 in the Greensboro Coliseum.</p>
<p>The Greensboro Coliseum has played host to many college basketball tournaments. The Atlantic Coast Conference has held their men's basketball tournament at the Coliseum 23 times since 1967, the most of any venue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> This is in part because the arena was within seven hours' drive of the conference's original footprint, and is within an hour of most of the fanbases of the conference's heartland in North Carolina. The Coliseum hosted the 2010 and 2011 men's tournament, and is scheduled to host four more ACC men's tournaments in 2013, 2014, &amp; 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> It has also hosted the <a href="/wiki/MEAC_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="MEAC Men's Basketball Tournament">MEAC Men's Basketball Tournament</a> ten times.</p>
<p>In 1974 the Coliseum hosted the NCAA Men's Final Four. It was the host of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Conference" title="Southern Conference">Southern Conference</a> men's basketball tournament from 1996 to 1999. The Coliseum has been the home for the <a href="/wiki/ACC_Women%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="ACC Women's Basketball Tournament">ACC Women's Basketball Tournament</a> since 2000, and is contracted through 2015. It has played host to 12 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">Men's NCAA Tournaments</a>, most notably the 1974 Final Four and Lehigh's upset of Duke in 2012. It hosted the NCAA Tournament in 2006 and 2009, when it served as a first and second round site. It hosted the Greensboro Regional in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="NCAA Women's Division I Basketball Tournament">Women's NCAA Tournament</a> in 2007 and 2008. The Coliseum is the first arena to host three basketball tournaments in consecutive weeks. The Coliseum has also hosted <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> basketball, high school basketball, and the <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Globetrotters" title="Harlem Globetrotters">Harlem Globetrotters</a>.</p>
<p>From 1959 to 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_Demon_Deacons" title="Wake Forest Demon Deacons">Wake Forest Demon Deacons</a> basketball team played a portion of its home schedule there—usually games against popular opponents that could not be accommodated in the smaller <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Winston-Salem Memorial Coliseum">Winston-Salem Memorial Coliseum</a>. The arena has also served as an alternate home floor for the <a href="/wiki/UNC_Greensboro_Spartans" title="UNC Greensboro Spartans">UNC Greensboro Spartans</a> men's basketball team, such as on December 31, 2005, when UNCG hosted top-ranked Duke at the Greensboro Coliseum in front of a near-record crowd of 21,124. Beginning with the 2009–2010 season, UNCG men's basketball team moved all its home games there from the cramped <a href="/wiki/Fleming_Gymnasium" title="Fleming Gymnasium">Fleming Gymnasium</a> on campus, which had been its home court since 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets" title="Charlotte Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</a> chose Greensboro for the location of their new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_Developmental_League" title="NBA Developmental League">NBA D-League</a> team the <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Swarm" title="Greensboro Swarm">Greensboro Swarm</a>. The Swarm will play at the Pavilion and debut in 2016-17 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greensboro_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greensboro-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 6th, 2016, the Hornets will play a preseason game against the Boston Celtics at Greensboro Coliseum.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indoor_football">Indoor football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Indoor football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Coliseum first saw an Arena Football team when the <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Prowlers" title="Greensboro Prowlers">Greensboro Prowlers</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Af2" title="Af2">af2</a> league played in the Coliseum from 1999 until 2004. The team folded due to a poor record and lack of fan support. The <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_Revolution" title="Greensboro Revolution">Greensboro Revolution</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Indoor_Football_League" title="National Indoor Football League">National Indoor Football League</a> played here in 2006 and 2007. The team ceased operations on January 23, 2008.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_events">Other events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greensboro_Coliseum_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Coliseum has hosted many events over time, including <a href="/wiki/Monster_Jam" title="Monster Jam">Monster Jam</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supercross" title="Supercross">Arenacross</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Bull_Riders" title="Professional Bull Riders">PBR</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical:_The_Concert" title="High School Musical: The Concert">High School Musical: The Concert</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ringling_Bros._and_Barnum_%26_Bailey_Circus" title="Ringling Bros. and Barnum &amp; Bailey Circus">Ringling Bros. and Barnum &amp; Bailey Circus</a>, and large-scale religious gatherings. It's also located between and within an hour's drive of North Carolina's five largest cities: Charlotte, Raleigh, Greensboro, Winston-Salem, and Durham.</p>
<p>Former North Carolina senator <a href="/wiki/Kay_Hagan" title="Kay Hagan">Kay Hagan</a> held her Senate Victory Party at the Special Events Center on November 4, 2008. The Greensboro Coliseum has also hosted the National Figure Skating Championships twice.</p>
<p>In addition, its neighboring auditorium and special events center have hosted concerts, trade shows, <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">broadway theatre</a> shows, and similar events. The auditorium, which was not included in the 1993 renovation of the complex, will soon be renovated to include a banquet hall. In 2002, the 1st Annual King of the Concrete indoor go-kart race was held at this facility. In February 2016, The Coliseum is scheduled to host the 2016 US Olympic Table Tennis Trials.</p>
<p>Greensboro Coliseum has had a wide history with hosting professional wrestling going back to the territorial days of <a href="/wiki/Jim_Crockett_Promotions" title="Jim Crockett Promotions">Jim Crockett Promotions</a>. It has hosted a number of <a href="/wiki/National_Wrestling_Alliance" title="National Wrestling Alliance">NWA</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Championship Wrestling">WCW</a> events through the years, including the first 4 <a href="/wiki/Starrcade" title="Starrcade">Starrcade</a> events in <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1983)" title="Starrcade (1983)">1983</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1984)" title="Starrcade (1984)">1984</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1985)" title="Starrcade (1985)">1985</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(1986)" title="Starrcade (1986)">1986</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/WrestleWar_(1990)" title="WrestleWar (1990)">1990 WrestleWar</a> event. <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a> has also held events at the Greensboro Coliseum, including <a href="/wiki/Unforgiven:_In_Your_House" title="Unforgiven: In Your House">Unforgiven: In Your House</a> in 1998, the <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Ring_(1999)" title="King of the Ring (1999)">1999 King of the Ring</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(2001)" title="Survivor Series (2001)">2001 Survivor Series</a> when Team WWF defeated Team Alliance and Alliance disbanded forever.</p>
<p>On April 8, 2016, just two days before his scheduled concert at the coliseum, musician <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> cancelled the show in protest of the passage of NC House Bill 2 (<a href="/wiki/Public_Facilities_Privacy_%26_Security_Act" title="Public Facilities Privacy &amp; Security Act">Public Facilities Privacy &amp; Security Act</a>). The legislation, signed by Governor <a href="/wiki/Pat_McCrory" title="Pat McCrory">Pat McCrory</a>, gained national attention for being discriminatory to specific groups based on gender identification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
